The Principle of Perpetuity in Binding Transactions and Its Application to the Safih
Stating a legal maxim and its application to the safih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a binding transaction requires capacity for its perpetuity as for its initiation, and apply it to explain why zakat and nafaqah remain obligatory on a safih.

Core Idea
For a binding transaction, the same capacity needed at its start is required for its continuation.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi maxim from the chapter of al-Ma'dhun: a binding legal act (tasarruf lazim) is treated, for its continuation, as if it were being initiated. This means that the capacity or eligibility required at the beginning must persist for the act to remain valid. The passage then applies this maxim to the case of a safih (a person interdicted due to foolish spending) — showing that obligations like zakat and family maintenance (nafaqah) are binding rights of Allah or of people, and the safih's lack of capacity does not nullify them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Maxim
Read the Arabic principle: 'ما يكون لازما من التصرف يعطى لدوامه حكم الابتداء'. Recognize that this is a general rule: a binding transaction (e.g., sale, marriage) is treated, for its continuation (dawam), as if it were being initiated (ibtida').
This maxim appears in the context of the authorized person (ma'dhun) but applies broadly.
2
Distinguish Binding vs Non-Binding Transactions
Understand that binding transactions (lazim) require capacity at initiation and perpetuity; non-binding transactions (ghayr lazim) require capacity only at the time of acting.
For example, a gift before delivery is non-binding; if the donor loses capacity after the offer, the gift may be revoked. But a sale is binding; if the buyer becomes insane after the contract, the sale remains valid.
3
Apply the Maxim to the Safih
The passage states that zakat and nafaqah are taken from the safih's wealth. This is because these are binding obligations (rights of Allah or of people). The safih is mukhatab (addressed by the Law) and his safah does not make him exempt.
The maxim operates here: the obligation to pay zakat was binding from the moment wealth reached nisab; the safih's later interdiction does not remove the obligation because the perpetuity of the binding duty requires the same capacity as initiation.
4
Understand that Safah Does Not Nullify Rights
The commentary clarifies that safah (foolishness) does not nullify the rights of people or the rights of Allah. The safih remains obligated for zakat, hajj, and nafaqah of dependents.
This reinforces the maxim: the binding nature of these obligations means they persist even if the person loses full capacity.

Source Text

كتاب المأذون
(۱۳۴) مَا يَكُونُ لَازِمًا مِنَ التَّصَرُّفِ يُعْطَى لِدَوَامِهِ حُكْمُ الْاِبْتِدَاءِ. )
ترجمہ: جو تصرف لازم ہو اس کے دوام کے لئے ابتداء کا حکم ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو تصرف لازم ہو اس کے دوام کے لئے اور بقاء کے لئے ابتداء کا حکم ہوتا ہے، یعنی ابتداء اہلبیت تو ضروری ہوتی ہے لیکن بقاء ضروری نہیں ہوتی ، اور جو تصرف لازم نہ ہو اس کے درست ہونے کے لئے حالت بقاء میں بھی اس تصرف کی اہلیت ضروری ہوگی۔
قَالَ (وَتُخْرَجُ الزَّكَاةُ مِنْ مَالِ السَّفِيهِ وَالْأَصْلُ فِي هَذِهِ الْمَسَائِلِ أَنَّ مَا وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ مِنْ أَمْرٍ أَوْجَبَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كَالزَّكَاةِ وَحَجَّةِ الْإِسْلَامِ، أَوْ كَانَ مِنْ حُقُوقِ النَّاسِ كَنَفَقَةِ مَنْ تَجِبُ نَفَقَتُهُ عَلَيْهِ فَهَذَا وَالْمُصْلِحُ فِيهِ سَوَاءٌ، لِأَنَّهُ مُخَاطَبٌ وَبِالسَّفَهِ لَا يَسْتَحِقُ النَّظَرَ فِي إِسْقَاطِ شَيْءٍ مِنْ حُقُوقِ الشَّرُعِ عَنْهُ، وَلَا يُبْطِلُ شَيْئًا مِنْ حُقُوقِ
النَّاس. (العناية كتاب الحجر، باب الحجر للفساد، ج ۹ ص۲۶۷)
وَتَخْرُجُ الزَّكَاةُ مِنْ مَالِ السَّفِيهِ وَيُنْفِقُ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى وَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ مَنْ تَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ نَفَقَتُهُ مِنْ ذَوِى أَرْحَامِهِ مِنْ مَالِهِ، لِأَنَّ إِحْيَاءَ وَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ مِنْ حَوَائِجِهِ الْأَصْلِيَّةِ وَالْإِنْفَاقُ عَلَى ذِى الرَّحِمِ الْمُحَرَّمِ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْهِ حَقًّا لِقَرَابَتِهِ وَالسَّفَهُ لَا يُبْطِلُ حُقُوق النَّاسِ وَلَا حُقُوق اللَّهِ تَعَالَى. تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الحجر، فصل حرمة
طرف الإنسان، ج ۵ ص ۱۹۷)
الهداية: كتاب المأذون، ج ۳ ص ٣٦٦
Chapter of the Authorized Person. (134) A transaction that is binding is given the ruling of initiation for its perpetuity. Translation: A binding transaction has the ruling of initiation for its perpetuity. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that for the perpetuity and continuation of a binding transaction, the ruling of initiation applies, i.e., eligibility at the beginning is necessary, but continuation is not necessary; and for a non-binding transaction, aptitude is necessary for its validity even in the state of continuation. He said: Zakat is taken from the wealth of the safih, and the principle in these issues is that whatever became obligatory upon him from a matter made obligatory by Allah Almighty, like zakat and the Hajj of Islam, or was from the rights of people, like nafaqah of those whose nafaqah is obligatory upon him, then this is the same as the one who rectifies [i.e., a sane person], because he is addressed [by the Law], and due to safah he does not deserve consideration in dropping any of the rights of the Sharia from him, and it does not nullify anything from the rights of people. (al-Inayah: Kitab al-Hajr, Bab al-Hajr li al-Fasad, vol. 9, p. 267). And zakat is taken from the wealth of the safih, and he spends upon himself, his child, and his wife, and those whose nafaqah is obligatory upon him from his relatives, because maintaining his child and wife is from his primary needs, and spending on a mahram relative is obligatory upon him as a right due to kinship, and safah does not nullify the rights of people nor the rights of Allah Almighty. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Hajr, Fasl Hurmatu Tarafi al-Insan, vol. 5, p. 197). al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Ma'dhun, vol. 3, p. 366.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct elements. First, it states a legal principle (qawida) from the chapter of al-Ma'dhun: a binding transaction (tasarruf lazim) is given the ruling of initiation for its perpetuity. This means that if a transaction is binding (e.g., a sale, marriage), the capacity or eligibility required at the time of its commencement is also required for its continuation; if the capacity is lost later, the transaction may be affected. For non-binding transactions, capacity is required throughout. Second, the passage includes a quote from al-Hidayah that reaffirms the principle from the previous lesson: zakat and nafaqah are taken from the property of a safih. This repetition ties the two chapters together. The quote explains that the safih is mukhatab (addressed by the Law) and his safah does not make him deserving of having obligations dropped. The passage ends with a citation from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq emphasizing that safah does not nullify rights of people or rights of Allah. Thus, the lesson encapsulates a general usul principle and its application to the specific case of the safih.

Key Terms
تصرف لازم (tasarruf lazim): A binding legal act that cannot be unilaterally revoked
دوام (dawam): Perpetuity or continuation of a legal act
ابتداء (ibtida'): Initiation or commencement of a legal act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle 'ما يكون لازما من التصرف يعطى لدوامه حكم الابتداء', what happens to a binding transaction if the party loses capacity after initiation?
A) The transaction is immediately void
B) The transaction continues regardless of capacity
C) The transaction is affected because the capacity needed for initiation is also needed for perpetuity
D) The transaction becomes optional

Key Takeaway
A binding transaction requires the same capacity for its continuation as for its initiation, and this principle ensures that the safih remains obligated for zakat and nafaqah.

Definition of Ghasb and Its Legal Effect
Definition of ghasb and application of a qawida

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ghasb and explain the legal consequence for the continuation of a permission-based contract when the owner loses capacity.

Core Idea
Ghasb is wrongful possession by removing the owner's physical control; contracts depend on capacity.

This lesson presents the precise Hanafi definition of ghasb (usurpation) as found in Al-Hidayah. The definition is concise but loaded with legal elements: establishment of possession, removal of the owner's hand, and a physical act on the property. The passage then applies a foundational qawida from the chapter on the ma'dhun slave: a non-binding contract requires capacity for its continuation. Understanding this definition is key to distinguishing ghasb from other forms of possession and to grasping the interplay between ownership, capacity, and contractual validity.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the definition
Recite the Arabic: الغصب إثبات اليد بإزالة يد المالك بفعل في العين. Break it into three components: ithbat al-yad (establishment of possession), izalat yad al-malik (removal of the owner's hand), and fi'l fi al-'ayn (an act on the property).
The term 'yad' (hand) here signifies legal possession or control, not physical body part.
2
Identify the three essential elements
For an action to be ghasb, it must: (1) establish possession by the usurper, (2) remove the owner's possession, and (3) involve a direct act on the property. Missing any element means the action is not ghasb.
For example, simply preventing the owner from using property without taking possession is not ghasb.
3
Recognize the applied qawida
The passage applies a rule from the ma'dhun chapter: a non-binding contract (like permission for trade) ceases if the party with capacity dies, becomes insane, or joins dar al-harb as an apostate. This shows that the continuation of permission requires the owner's legal capacity.
The contract is 'ghayr lazim' (non-binding), so its persistence depends on ongoing capacity.
4
Derive the legal effect for the ma'dhun slave
If the master dies or becomes insane, the slave becomes mahjur (restricted) because the permission is void. The reasoning: the contract was not binding, so it ends when the owner loses capacity. This prevents the slave from trading.
This illustrates how a qawida is applied across different chapters of fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الغصب
(۱۳۵) اَلْغَصَبُ إِثْبَاتُ الْيَدِ بِإِزَالَةِ يَدِ الْمَالِكِ بِفِعْلِ فِي الْعَيْنِ. قَالَ: (وَلَوْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى أَوْ جُنَّ ، أَوْ لَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ مُرْتَدَّا صَارَ مَحْجُورًا ) لأَنَّهُ زَالَ مِلْكُهُ عَنْهُ بِالْمَوْتِ وَالصَّحَاقِ، أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ يَنْتَقِلُ إِلَى مِلْكِ وَرَثَتِهِ وَهُوَ عَقْدٌ غَيْرُ لَازِمٍ فَيَزُولُ بِزَوَالِ الْمِلْكِ، وَبِالْجُنُونِ زَالَتِ الْأَهْلِيَّةُ فَيَبْطُلُ الْإِذْنُ اعْتِبَارًا بِالابْتِدَاءِ، لِأَنَّ مَا يَلْزَمُ مِنَ التَّصَرُّفَاتِ يُعْتَبَرُ لِدَوَامِهِ الْأَهْلِيَّةُ كَمَا يُعْتَبَرُ لابتدائه. (الاختيار لتعليل المختار: كتاب المأذون، ج ۲ ص ۱۰۳) قَالَ وَلَوْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى أَوْ جُنَّ أَوْ لَحِقَ بِدَارِ الْحَرْبِ قَدْ تَقَدَّمَ أَنَّ التَّصَرُّفَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لَازِمًا كَانَ لِدَوَامِهِ حُكْمُ ابْتِدَائِهِ فَيَحْتَاجُ إِلَى قِيَامِ الْأَهْلِيَّةِ حَالَةَ الْبَقَاءِ كَالِابْتِدَاء. (العناية: كتاب المأذون، ج ۹ ص ۲۹۶)
الهداية كتاب الغصب، ج ۳ ص ۳۷٤
Book of Ghasb. (135) Ghasb is the establishment of hand (possession) by removing the hand of the owner through an act on the property. He said: And if the master dies, becomes insane, or goes to dar al-harb as an apostate, he becomes restricted, because his ownership ceases from him due to death and joining dar al-harb, do you not see that it transfers to the ownership of his heirs, and it is a non-binding contract, so it ceases with the cessation of ownership, and with insanity capacity ceases, so the permission becomes invalid by analogy with the inception, because for what is binding from transactions, capacity is considered for its continuation just as it is considered for its inception. (Al-Ikhtiyar li Ta'lil al-Mukhtar: Kitab al-Ma'dhun, vol. 2 p. 103). He said: And if the master dies, becomes insane, or goes to dar al-harb, it has preceded that if a transaction is not binding, then for its continuation the ruling of its inception applies, so it requires the presence of capacity in the state of persistence like inception. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Ma'dhun, vol. 9 p. 296). Al-Hidayah Kitab al-Ghasb, vol. 3 p. 374.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This is a definition passage from the beginning of the chapter on ghasb (usurpation) in Al-Hidayah. The definition is concise: ghasb is the establishment of possession by removing the owner's hand through a physical act on the property. This means the usurper takes control of the property in a way that excludes the owner, typically by force or without right. The passage then applies the earlier qawida about necessary transactions to the case of a ma'dhun slave, showing that the same principle applies in the context of ghasb: if the master dies or becomes insane, the slave becomes restricted. The quote from Al-Hidayah Kitab al-Ghasb indicates that this discussion is part of the ghasb chapter, though it references the ma'dhun. The point is that the permission (idhn) for trade is a non-binding contract, so its continuation requires the master's capacity. This definition and application serve as a foundation for understanding ghasb and its connection to capacity in contracts.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): The wrongful taking of property by physically removing the owner's possession.
اثبات اليد (ithbat al-yad): Establishing possession or control over property.
ازالة يد المالك (izalat yad al-malik): Removing the owner's hand, i.e., depriving the owner of possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition, what constitutes ghasb?
A) Any unlawful possession.
B) Establishing possession by removing the owner's hand through an act on the property.
C) Simply taking someone's property without permission.
D) Possession that lasts more than a day.

Key Takeaway
Ghasb is defined as the wrongful establishment of possession by physically removing the owner's control over property; the continuation of a permission-based contract requires the owner's legal capacity.

Definition of Ghasb and Its Application to Immovable Property
Defines ghasb and applies definition to immovable property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definition of ghasb and apply it to determine whether a usurper is liable for natural destruction of immovable property.

Core Idea
Ghasb requires a physical act on the object; land cannot be 'ghasb' strictly, so natural destruction does not create liability.

This passage from al-Hidayah examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: if someone wrongfully occupies land and it is destroyed by a flood, is he liable? The answer turns on the precise definition of ghasb. We will explore how Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf distinguish movable from immovable property, and why Imam Muhammad differs.

Guided Path
1
Define ghasb per Hanafi school
Identify the two essential elements: removal of owner's hand (izalat yad al-malik) and establishment of usurper's hand (ithbat al-yad) through a physical act on the object.
The definition is from the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
2
Apply definition to immovable property
Show why removal of owner's hand is impossible by an act on the object itself; possession of land ends only by eviction, which is an act on the owner's person, not on the property.
Eviction (ikhraj) is an act on the owner, not on the land.
3
State the ruling of the two Shaykhs
Because ghasb is not realized, liability (daman) does not attach for destruction without the usurper's act.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
4
Present Imam Muhammad's opposing view
He holds that the usurper is liable even for natural destruction, based on wrongful possession (yad al-mutaghalliba) regardless of the precise definition.
Imam Muhammad does not require the act to be on the object itself.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that of the two Shaykhs, as supported by Al-Inayah and later Hanafi authorities.
This is the ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: غصب عین میں فعل کے ذریعے مالک کے قبضے کو زائل کر کے قبضہ ثابت کرنے کا نام ہے۔ تشریح مذکور و اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شیخین رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک غصب کا معنی ہے کہ غاصب شے مغصوبہ میں فعل غصب کے ذریعے مالک کے قبضے کو زائل کر کے اپنا قبضہ ثابت کرے، اور یہ صرف منقولی چیزوں میں ہو سکتا ہے، غیر منقولی چیز میں یہ معنی متفق نہیں ہوسکتا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ اگر غاصب نے زمین غصب کی اور وہ زمین کسی آفت سماوی سے ہلاک ہوگئی، تو غاصب شیخین رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک ضامن نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ غصب کا معنی ہے مغصو بہ شے میں فعل غصب سرانجام دے کر مالک کے قبضے کو زائل کرنا اور غصب کی یہ تعریف عقار پر صادق نہیں آتی ، کیونکہ عقار سے اسی وقت مالک کا قبضہ ختم ہوگا جب مالک کو عقار سے بے دخل کر دیا جائے اور یہ بے دخلی مالک کی ذات میں تصرف ہوگا نہ کہ زمین میں اور جب مغصوبہ زمین میں غصب مؤثر نہیں ہوگا تو غصب محقق بھی نہیں ہوگا اور جب غصب متحقق نہیں ہوگا تو اس زمین کی ہلاکت سے غاصب پر ضمان نہیں ہوگا۔ (فَإِذَا غَصَبَ عَقَارًا فَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ بِغَيْرِ صُنْعِهِ لَمْ يَضْمَنْهُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ. وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ يَضْمَنُهُ.... وَلَابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّ الْغَصْبَ إِثْبَاتُ الْيَدِ بِإِزَالَةِ يَدِ الْمَالِكِ) أَيْ بِسَبَبٍ ذَلَكَ (وَهَذَا) أَيْ هَذَا الْمَجُمُوعُ وَلَا يُتَصَوَّرُ فِي الْعَقَارِ، لِأَنَّ يَدَ الْمَالِكِ لَا تَزُولُ إِلَّا بِإِخْرَاجِهِ) أَى بِإِخْرَاجِ الْمَالِكِ عَنْهَا) أَيْ عَنْ الْعَقَارِ بِمَعْنَى الضَّيْعَةِ أَوْ الدَّارِ (وَهُوَ أَى الْإِخْرَاجُ فِعْلٌ فِي الْمَالِكِ لَا فِي الْعَقَارِ) فَانْتَفَى إِزَالَةُ الْيَدِ وَالْكُلُّ يَنْتَفِي بِانْتِفَاءِ جُزْئِهِ. (العناية: كتاب الغصب، ج ۹ ص ۳۲۳)
Translation: Ghasb is the establishment of possession by removing the owner's possession through an act in the object itself. Explanation of the aforementioned principle: According to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), ghasb means that the usurper removes the owner's possession from the usurped object through an act of usurpation and establishes his own possession. This can only occur in movable property; in immovable property, this meaning cannot be realized. The author of Hidayah, after mentioning the principle, states that if someone usurps land and it perishes in his hand due to a natural calamity, then according to the two Shaykhs, the usurper is not liable. Because ghasb means removing the owner's possession by performing an act of usurpation in the object, and this definition does not apply to immovable property. Because in immovable property, the owner's possession only ceases when he is evicted, and this eviction is an act upon the owner, not upon the land. So when the act of usurpation is not effective in the usurped land, then ghasb is not realized, and when ghasb is not realized, no liability for its destruction falls on the usurper. (For if he usurps immovable property and it perishes in his hand without his act, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say he is not liable. Muhammad says he is liable.... For Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, ghasb is the establishment of possession by removal of the owner's possession – meaning through that cause – and this totality is not conceivable in immovable property, because the owner's possession does not cease except by his eviction – meaning removal of the owner from it – and that eviction is an act upon the owner, not upon the immovable property. Therefore, the removal of possession is negated, and the whole is negated by the negation of its part. (Al-Inayah: Kitab al-Ghasb, vol. 9 p. 323)
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the liability of a usurper of immovable property (like land or a house) that is destroyed by a natural disaster without the usurper's fault. The definition of ghasb is first established: it requires (1) removal of the owner's hand (yad al-malik) and (2) establishment of the usurper's hand on the object through a physical act. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two Shaykhs) argue that this definition cannot apply to immovable property (aqar). For land or buildings, the owner's possession is not a physical holding but a legal right that is only lost when the owner is physically evicted. Eviction is an act on the owner's person, not on the property itself. Since the act of usurpation (taking possession) is not directed at the property, the definition of ghasb is not fulfilled. Therefore, if the property perishes by an act of God, the usurper is not liable because he is not considered a usurper in the full sense. Imam Muhammad disagrees, holding that the usurper is liable. The commentary explains that the relied-upon view is that of the two Shaykhs, as supported by Al-Inayah. This ruling reflects the Hanafi emphasis on the precise meaning of ghasb as a physical removal of the owner's hand from the object itself.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Establishing possession of another's property by removing the owner's possession through a physical act.
عقار (aqar): Immovable property such as land and buildings.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if someone wrongfully takes land and it is destroyed by a flood without his fault, is he liable?
A) Yes, because he is a usurper.
B) No, because ghasb of immovable property is not established as there is no act on the land itself.
C) Yes, if he had built on it.
D) No, only if he returns the land.

Key Takeaway
Ghasb of immovable property is not established under the Hanafi definition, so the usurper is not liable for natural destruction without his act.

The Pre-emptor is like a Buyer
States the principle of legal parity between pre-emptor and buyer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that the pre-emptor is legally equivalent to a buyer and apply it to determine the pre-emptor's rights to options of inspection and defect.

Core Idea
The pre-emptor stands in the buyer's shoes — same rights, same options.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle in Hanafi pre-emption law: the pre-emptor (shafī') is treated like a buyer (mushtarī). This means that when a judge awards the property to the pre-emptor, the pre-emptor enjoys the same contractual options as a buyer — namely, the option of inspection (khiyār al-ru'yah) and the option of defect (khiyār al-'ayb). Even if the original buyer waived his right to claims defects, that waiver does not bind the pre-emptor because the pre-emptor's right is independent.

Guided Path
1
State the Principle
Recite the core maxim: 'Taking by pre-emption is like purchase.' This means the pre-emptor is legally treated as a buyer.
Memorize the Arabic: الأخُذُ بِالشُّفْعَةِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الشَّرَاءِ.
2
Identify the Consequences
Since the pre-emptor is like a buyer, he gets the same options that a buyer has in a sale contract.
Focus on the two options mentioned: khiyār al-ru'yah and khiyār al-'ayb.
3
Apply Option of Inspection (Khiyār al-Ru'yah)
If the pre-emptor had not seen the property before the judge's decision, he may return it after seeing it if dissatisfied.
This mirrors the buyer's right to return an unseen item.
4
Apply Option of Defect (Khiyār al-'Ayb)
If the pre-emptor discovers a defect that existed at the time of sale, he may return the property, even if the original buyer had waived defects.
The pre-emptor's right is independent; the buyer cannot forfeit it.
5
Note the Independence
The pre-emptor is not the buyer's agent, so the buyer's actions (like waiving defects) do not affect the pre-emptor's rights.
This emphasizes the protective nature of pre-emption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة
باب طلب الشفعة والخصومة فيها
(1) الأخُذُ بِالشُّفْعَةِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الشَّرَاءِ.
ترجمہ شفع کے ذریعہ لینا یہ شراء کے ذریعے لینے کی مانند ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شفعہ کے ذریعہ گھر یا زمین کو لینا ایسا ہی ہے جیسا کہ مشتری بائع سے شراء کے ذریعے لیتا ہے یعنی شفیع بمنزلہ مشتری کے ہے، لہذا جو
احکامات شراء کے ہیں وہ شفعہ میں بھی ملحوظ ہوں گی۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکور و اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ جس طرح دیکھے بغیر کوئی چیز خرید نے کے بعد اس میں عیب نظر آنے کی صورت میں مشتری کو خیار عیب اور خیاور ویت ملتا ہے ٹھیک اسی طرح جب قاضی شفعہ کی بنیاد پر شفیع کے لئے گھر کا فیصلہ کر لے اور شفیع نے گھر نہ دیکھا ہوتو شفیع کو بھی خیار رؤیت حاصل ہوگا، اسی طرح عیب کی وجہ سے شفیع واپس بھی کر سکتا ہے، اگر چہ مشتری نے عیوب سے براءت کی شرط لگائی ہو، کیونکہ شفیع بمنزلہ مشتری کے ہے اور مشتری نے اگر چہ گھر دیکھا نہ ہو تو بھی اس کو خیار رؤیت حاصل ہوتا ہے، لہذا شفیع کو بھی خیار رویت حاصل
ہوگا، اسی طرح مشتری کو خیار عیب حاصل ہوتا ہے، لہذ ا شفیع کو بھی خیار عیب حاصل ہوگا۔ الهداية كتاب الشفعة، باب طلب الشفعة والخصومة فيها، ج ۳ ص ۳۹۸ (قوله: وإذا قضى القاضى للشفيع بالدار ولم يكن رآها فله خيار الرؤية) لأن الشفيع بمنزلة المشترى فكما يجوز للمشترى أن يردها بخيار الرؤية، والعيب فكذا الشفيع (قوله وإن وجد بها عيبا فله أن يردها، وإن كان المشترى شرط البراءة منه لأن المشترى ليس بنائب عنه فلا يملك إسقاط حق الشفيع.
(الجوهرة النيرة كتاب الشفعة، ح ا ص ۲۸۴
Book of Pre-emption
Chapter on Seeking Pre-emption and Litigation Therein
(1) Taking by pre-emption is like purchase.
Translation: Taking through shuf'ah is like taking through purchase.
Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that taking a house or land through pre-emption is just like how the buyer takes from the seller through purchase, i.e., the pre-emptor is in the position of the buyer. Therefore, the rulings that apply to purchase will also be observed in pre-emption.
The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to show that just as when a person buys something without seeing it and then finds a defect, he has the option of defect and option of inspection, likewise when the judge decides the house in favor of the pre-emptor based on pre-emption and the pre-emptor has not seen the house, then the pre-emptor will also have the option of inspection. Similarly, he can return it due to defect, even if the buyer had stipulated exemption from defects, because the pre-emptor is in the position of the buyer, and if the buyer has not seen the house, he still has the option of inspection; therefore, the pre-emptor will also have the option of inspection. Similarly, the buyer has the option of defect, so the pre-emptor will also have the option of defect. Al-Hidayah, Book of Shuf'ah, Chapter on Seeking Pre-emption and Litigation Therein, vol. 3 p. 398 (His saying: And when the judge decides the house in favor of the pre-emptor and he had not seen it, he has the option of inspection) because the pre-emptor is in the position of the buyer, so just as it is permissible for the buyer to return it due to option of inspection and defect, so too the pre-emptor. (His saying: And if he finds a defect in it, he has the right to return it, even if the buyer had stipulated exemption from it because the buyer is not his agent, so he cannot waive the right of the pre-emptor. (Al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, Book of Shuf'ah, part 1 p. 284)
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage introduces the key principle in Hanafi law of pre-emption (shuf'ah): 'Taking by pre-emption is like purchase.' This means the pre-emptor (shafī') is legally treated as a buyer (mushtarī) when he exercises his right to take the property from the buyer. The practical consequence is that the pre-emptor enjoys the same contractual options that a buyer would have: the option of inspection (khiyār al-ru'yah) and the option of defect (khiyār al-'ayb). Even if the original buyer had waived his right to claim defects, that waiver does not bind the pre-emptor because the pre-emptor is not the buyer's agent and the buyer cannot forfeit the pre-emptor's independent right. The passage from Al-Hidayah explicitly states that when the judge awards the property to the pre-emptor, if the pre-emptor had not seen it, he can return it upon seeing a defect. This illustrates the comprehensive nature of the pre-emptor's rights within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of a neighbor or co-owner to take possession of sold property by paying the price, preventing a stranger from acquiring it.
خيار الرؤية (khiyār al-ru'yah): The option of inspection: the right to return an item if it was bought without seeing it and the buyer is dissatisfied upon seeing it.
خيار العيب (khiyār al-'ayb): The option of defect: the right to return an item if a defect is discovered that existed at the time of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in the passage, what right does a pre-emptor have if he finds a defect in the property after the judge awards it to him?
A) He cannot return it because the judge already decided.
B) He can return it only if the original buyer had also returned it.
C) He can return it due to the option of defect, even if the buyer had waived defects.
D) He can return it only if the seller agrees.

Key Takeaway
The pre-emptor is legally like a buyer, enjoying the same options of inspection and defect, and the buyer's waiver does not affect this right.

5 min
Annulment of Sale Does Not Nullify Pre-emption Right
Clarifies that the shafi's right persists even if the sale is annulled.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that faskh al-bay' does not nullify haqq al-shafi' and explain the scenario where this principle is applied.

Core Idea
Faskh al-bay' does not nullify haqq al-shafi'.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental principle of shuf'ah: the annulment of a sale contract between seller and buyer does not affect the pre-emptor's right. The shafi' retains his claim even when a judge dissolves the sale due to a dispute. Through a concrete scenario, we see how this rule protects the pre-emptor from being disadvantaged by conflicts between the parties to the sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal effect stated
The principle clearly states that faskh al-bay' does not nullify haqq al-shafi'. Recognize that this is a rule about the persistence of a right, not about creating or destroying it.
The right is independent of the contractual relationship.
2
Note the condition for application
The shafi' must have had a valid pre-emption right at the time of the original sale. Without that, faskh is irrelevant.
Condition is that the right attached before the annulment.
3
Examine the illustrative scenario
When seller and buyer dispute the price and both take oaths, the judge dissolves the sale. Yet the shafi' still takes the house at the seller's claimed price. This shows that the right survives judicial annulment.
The scenario is from Hidayah, showing practical application.
4
Understand the rationale
The shafi's right is a property right that attaches from the moment of sale, not a contractual obligation contingent on the sale's continuation. Therefore, dissolution of the contract does not erase the right.
This distinguishes shuf'ah from mere contractual claims.

Source Text

اصول ہدایہ رائج
(۲) فَسُخُ الْبَيْعِ لَا يُوجِبُ بُطَلانَ حَقِّ الشَّفِيعِ. ترجمہ بیج کا شیخ ہو ناحق قطیع کے بطلان کو ثابت نہیں کرتا ۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان بیچ شیخ ہو جائے تو اس سے شفیع کا حق باطل نہ ہوگا بلکہ شفیع کو بدستور شفعہ کا حق حاصل ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر بائع اور مشتری کاشن میں اختلاف ہو جائے اور بائع مشتری سے زیادہ شمن کا دعوی کرے تو دونوں قسمیں کھائیں گے، اگر کسی ایک نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو جس نے قسم کھائی اس کے قول کا اعتبار ہوگا، لہذا شفیع اسی قیمت پر گھر لے گا اور اگر دونوں نے قسمیں کھا لیں تو قاضی بیچ کو فتح کر دے اور شفیع بائع کے قول کے مطابق شفعہ کے ذریعہ گھر لے گا، کیونکہ مذکورہ صورت میں قاضی نے بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان بیچ کو ضبح کردیا اور صبح پیچ شفیع کے حق کو باطل نہیں کر سکتا، لہذا مذکورہ صورت میں بھی فسخ بیع سے شفیع کا حق باطل نہ ہو گا۔
(قال: وإذا قضى للشفيع بالدار ولم يكن رآها فله خيار الرؤية) أى قال القدورى قوله: ولم يكن أى والحال أنه قال لم يكن رآها قبل ذلك (وإن وجد بها عيبا فله أن يردها) أى وإن وجد الشفيع بالدار عيبا له أن يردها لأن الشفيع مع المشترى بمنزلة المشترى أن البائع ثم المشترى له أن يرد بخيار الرؤية والعيب، فكذلك للشفيع أن يرد بالخيارين على الذى أخذ منه . وإن كان المشترى شرط البراءة منه أى من العيب لأن الأخذ بالشفعة بمنزلة الشراء). البناية كتاب الشفعة، باب طلب الشفعة والخصومة فيها، ج ا ا ص ٣٢٠) الهداية كتاب الشفعة، باب طلب الشفعة والخصومة فيها، فصل في الاختلاف، ج ۴ ص ۳۹۹ وَلَوِ اخْتَلَفَ الْبَائِعُ مَعَ الْمُشْتَرِى وَالشَّفِيعِ وَالدَّارُ فِي يَدِ الْبَائِعِ أَوْ الْمُشْتَرِى
The dissolution of the sale does not necessitate the nullification of the right of the pre-emptor. Translation: The dissolution of the sale does not prove the nullification of the right of the pre-emptor. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that if the sale between the seller and buyer becomes annulled, the right of the pre-emptor does not become void; rather, the pre-emptor continues to have the right of pre-emption. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a dispute arises between seller and buyer regarding the price, and the seller claims a higher price than the buyer, both take oaths. If one refuses to take an oath, the statement of the one who takes the oath is given weight, and the pre-emptor takes the house at that price. If both take oaths, the judge dissolves the sale, and the pre-emptor takes the house through pre-emption according to the seller's statement, because in this case the judge dissolved the sale between seller and buyer, and the dissolution of sale cannot nullify the right of the pre-emptor. Thus, in such a case, the dissolution of sale does not void the pre-emptor's right. (He said: And when he decrees the house for the pre-emptor and he had not seen it, he has the option of inspection) meaning Al-Quduri said: his statement 'he had not' meaning the case that he had not seen it before. (And if he finds a defect in it, he may return it) meaning if the pre-emptor finds a defect in the house, he may return it, because the pre-emptor with the buyer is in the position of the buyer, then the buyer has the right to return by option of inspection and defect, so similarly the pre-emptor has the right to return by both options against the one from whom he took. Even if the buyer stipulated waiver from it, meaning from the defect, because taking by pre-emption is like purchasing. (Al-Binayah, Kitab al-Shuf'ah, Bab Talab al-Shuf'ah wa al-Khusumah fiha, vol. 1, p. 320) (Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Shuf'ah, Bab Talab al-Shuf'ah wa al-Khusumah fiha, Fasl fi al-Ikhtilaf, vol. 4, p. 399) And if the seller disagrees with the buyer and the pre-emptor, and the house is in the possession of the seller or buyer...
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage presents the second principle of shuf'ah: the annulment (faskh) of the sale between seller and buyer does not nullify the shafi's right. The commentary illustrates with a scenario where seller and buyer dispute the price: if they both take conflicting oaths, the judge dissolves the sale, but the shafi still gets the house at the seller's claimed price. The reason is that the shafi's right is independent and not contingent on the continued existence of the sale. The Arabic quotes at the end are from Al-Binayah and Al-Hidayah, repeating the earlier principle about options of inspection and defect, showing consistency.

Key Terms
فسخ البيع (faskh al-bay'): The annulment or dissolution of a sale contract by a judge due to irresolvable dispute between seller and buyer.
حق الشفيع (haqq al-shafi'): The right of the pre-emptor to acquire the sold property, which remains intact even if the underlying sale is dissolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a seller and buyer dispute the price and both take oaths, leading the judge to dissolve the sale, what happens to the pre-emptor's right?
A) It becomes void because the sale is annulled
B) It remains, and he takes the house at the seller's claimed price
C) He loses it because oaths nullify pre-emption
D) He must wait for a new sale

Key Takeaway
The annulment of a sale does not nullify the pre-emptor's right; the shafi' continues to have a valid claim.

Partial Reduction of Price and Its Effect on Shafi'
Explaining the legal principle of partial reduction in price and its effect on shafi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that partial reduction of price attaches to the original contract when determining the shafi's payment.

Core Idea
A partial reduction of price retroactively sets the contract price; a full reduction does not bind the shafi'.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a seller reduces part of the price after the sale, this reduction is considered to have been part of the original contract. This principle directly affects the pre-emptor (shafi'), who takes the property at the effective price. However, if the seller forgives the entire price, the reduction does not retroact—the shafi' must still pay the original price. This lesson unpacks the rule and its application in disputes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the key terms
Identify the Arabic terms: hatt (reduction), shuf'a (pre-emption), thaman (price). Note the distinction between partial and full reduction.
Partial = hatt al-ba'd, full = hatt al-kull.
2
Grasp the core principle
The rule: partial reduction attaches to the original contract (yaltaḥiqu bi aṣl al-'aqd). That means the contract is retroactively amended to the reduced price.
Full reduction does not attach because it would negate the price.
3
Apply to the shafi' scenario
If the seller reduces part of the price, the shafi' also pays only that reduced amount. If the seller reduces the entire price, the shafi' still pays the original price.
The shafi' takes the property at the same price the buyer would have paid.
4
Handle disputes about the price
When the price has not been paid and the seller and buyer differ, the seller's statement is taken as the basis for what the shafi' pays.
The seller and buyer take oaths and return the property; the shafi' chooses to take at the seller's stated price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حَطَّ الْبَعْضِ يَلْتَحِقُ بِأَصْلِ الْعَقْدِ بِخِلَافِ حَطِ الْكُلّ. ترجمہ بعض شمن کا کم کرنا اصل عقد کے ساتھ لاحق ہوگا بر خلاف کل شمن کے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر عقد کے بعد بائع مشتری سے شمن میں سے کچھ من کم کر دے تو یہ کی اصل عقد کے ساتھ ملحق ہوگی، یعنی گویا کہ اصل عقد اسی شمن پر واقع ہوا تھا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر بائع نے مشتری سے بعض شمن کم کر دیا تو یہ شفیع سے بھی ساقط ہوگا کیونکہ ثمن وہی ہے جو باقی ہے، یعنی شفیع بھی وہی کم شمن دے کر دار مشفوعہ کو لے گا، اور اگر بائع نے کل ثمن چھوڑ دیا تو شفیع سے کل ثمن ساقط نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ بعض شمن کی کمی اصل عقد سے ملحق ہوتی ہے مکمل شمن کی نہیں، پید ا شفیع کے حق میں لَكِنَّهُ لَمْ يَنْقُدُ الثَّمَنَ فَالْقَوْلُ فِي ذَلِكَ قَوْلُ الْبَائِعِ، وَالْبَائِعُ مَعَ الْمُشْتَرِى يَتَحَالَفَانِ وَيَتَرَادَّان، وَالشَّفِيعُ يَأْخُذُ الدَّارَ بِمَا قَالَ الْبَائِعُ إِنْ شَاءَ. (بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الشفعة، فصل في اختلاف الشفيع والمشتري، ج ۵ ص ۳۱) قَالَ (وَإِذَا ادَّعَى الْمُشْتَرِى ثَمَنًا وَادَّعَى الْبَائِعُ أَقَلَّ مِنْهُ إِلَخَ) إِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الْبَائِعُ وَالْمُشْتَرِى فِى الثَّمَنِ فَإِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَقْبُوضًا أَوْ غَيْرَ مَقْبُوضٍ، أَوْ يَكُونَ الْقَبْضُ غَيْرَ ظَاهِرٍ : يَعْنِي غَيْرَ مَعْلُومٍ لِلشَّفِيعِ، فَإِنْ كَانَ غَيْرَ مَقْبُوضٍ فَإِمَّا أَنْ يَدَّعِيَ الْبَائِعُ أَقَلَّ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ ، فَإِنْ كَانَ أَقَلَّ أَخَذَهَا الشَّفِيعُ بِمَا قَالَ الْبَائِعُ وَكَانَ ذَلِكَ حَقًّا عَنِ
الْمُشْتَرِى. (العناية كتاب الشفعة، فصل في الاختلاف، ج ۹ ص ۳۹۲) الهداية كتاب الشفعة طلب الشفعة والخصومة فيها، فصل فيما يوخذ به المشفوع، ج۴ ص ۴۰۰
Reduction of part [of the price] attaches to the original contract, contrary to reduction of all. Translation: Reducing some of the price attaches to the original contract, unlike reducing the entire price. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if after the contract the seller reduces some of the price from the buyer, then it attaches to the original contract, meaning it is as if the original contract was concluded at that reduced price. The author of Al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that if the seller reduced some of the price from the buyer, then it is also dropped from the shafi' because the price is what remains; i.e., the shafi' will also take the property by paying that reduced price. And if the seller forewent the entire price, then the entire price is not dropped from the shafi', because reduction of part attaches to the original contract, not full reduction. Hence, for the shafi', but he did not pay the price, so the statement in that regard is the statement of the seller, and the seller and the buyer take an oath and return [the property], and the shafi' takes the house at what the seller says if he wishes. (Bada'i' al-Sana'i': Book of Shuf'a, Chapter on Dispute between Shafi' and Buyer, vol. 5 p. 31) He said: 'And when the buyer claims a price and the seller claims less than it, etc.' If the seller and buyer differ over the price, then either it has been received or not, or the receipt is not apparent, meaning unknown to the shafi'. If it has not been received, then either the seller claims less or more. If he claims less, the shafi' takes it at what the seller said, and that is a right from the buyer. (Al-'Inayah: Book of Shuf'a, Chapter on Disputes, vol. 9 p. 392) Al-Hidayah: Book of Shuf'a, Claiming Shuf'a and Litigation Therein, Chapter on What the Pre-empted Property is Taken For, vol. 4 p. 400
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of a seller reducing the price after the contract of sale, specifically in the context of shuf'a (pre-emption). The key principle is that a partial reduction of the price (hatt al-ba'd) is considered to attach to the original contract (yaltaḥiqu bi aṣl al-'aqd). This means that the reduction retroactively affects the contract price, as if the sale was always at the reduced price. Consequently, the shafi' (pre-emptor) also benefits from this reduction: the shafi' pays only the remaining price to take the property. In contrast, if the seller reduces the entire price (hatt al-kull), this does not attach to the original contract, because that would nullify the contract's subject matter (price). Therefore, the full price is still owed from the shafi'. The text also discusses a scenario where the price has not been paid and the seller and buyer differ on the amount; the seller's statement is given weight in determining what the shafi' must pay, following the principle that the seller's word is taken regarding the price when not paid. This ruling is based on the principle that the shafi' takes the property at the same price as the buyer would have paid, but only the reduced price if the reduction is partial. The authority weight is from Al-Hidayah, which is a core text of the Hanafi madhhab, and the ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms
حط (hatt): Reduction or remission of part or all of the price by the seller after the contract.
شفعة (shuf'a): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbour to purchase property sold to a third party by paying the price.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid for the property in the sale contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the seller reduces half of the price after the sale, what is the effect on the shafi's payment?
A) The shafi' must pay the original full price.
B) The shafi' pays the reduced price, as if the sale was at that price.
C) The shafi' does not have to pay anything.
D) The shafi' pays the original price but can claim the reduction from the seller.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a partial reduction of price retroactively becomes the contract price, binding on the shafi', while a full reduction does not affect the shafi's obligation.
